Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Steps to reproduce the problem:



<b class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce the problem:<!----></b>



<br>





To reproduce the problem, follow the provided testcase (issue_147992_f.html). Please note that the crash might not occur immediately. If this happens, reloading the testcase several times may lead to the crash. For instance, during my testing on macOS, the crash occurred after the third reload. The crash has been verified on stable versions of Linux, Windows, and macOS with code 11.



<span class="line"><!---->To reproduce the problem, follow the provided testcase (issue_147992_f.html). Please note that the crash might not occur immediately. If this happens, reloading the testcase several times may lead to the crash. For instance, during my testing on macOS, the crash occurred after the third reload. The crash has been verified on stable versions of Linux, Windows, and macOS with code 11.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Problem Description:



<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





The problem pertains to the crashing of the renderer process which leads to a segmentation fault.



<span class="line"><!---->The problem pertains to the crashing of the renderer process which leads to a segmentation fault.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I am currently in the process of preparing a full report inclusive of a stacktrace and an AddressSanitizer report, which will be provided in the comments once ready. Initial analysis suggests that this problem might be linked to the following commits: 



<span class="line"><!---->I am currently in the process of preparing a full report inclusive of a stacktrace and an AddressSanitizer report, which will be provided in the comments once ready. Initial analysis suggests that this problem might be linked to the following commits: <!----></span>

I was able to reproduce, and have a fix here:



<span class="line"><!---->I was able to reproduce, and have a fix here:<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





crrev.com/c/4669533



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/4669533"><!---->crrev.com/c/4669533<!----></a>





.



<span class="line"><!---->.<!----></span>





 It fixes the issue (at least on my side), but I think the issue is broader than this with `ClipboardPromise`: indeed, when the context is destroyed, the promise clears the its pointer to the writer. However, since the writer has a self keep alive, it doesn't do anything until it finishes loading the blob. I think we might be able to add a cancellation feature likewise what's being done in `FileReader`. That way, when the context is destroyed, we just cancel loading the blob.



<span class="line"><!----> It fixes the issue (at least on my side), but I think the issue is broader than this with `ClipboardPromise`: indeed, when the context is destroyed, the promise clears the its pointer to the writer. However, since the writer has a self keep alive, it doesn't do anything until it finishes loading the blob. I think we might be able to add a cancellation feature likewise what's being done in `FileReader`. That way, when the context is destroyed, we just cancel loading the blob.<!----></span>

Dear owner, thanks for fixing this bug. We’ve reopened it because security bugs need Security_Severity and FoundIn labels set, which will enable the bots to request merges to the correct branches ( as well as helping out our vulnerability reward and CVE processes). Please consult with any Chrome security contact (

Please consult with any Chrome security contact (<!----></span>





security@chromium.org
